                                  function simpleMask(str, key) {
                                      var result = ''; 
                                      for (var i = 0; i < str.length; ++i)
                                          result += String.fromCharCode(key ^ str.charCodeAt(i));
                                      return result;
                                  }

               <div class="msg-210x60" data-format="210x60" data-type="ad" data-publisher="lqm.codeproject.site" data-zone="General-Programming/Algorithms-Recipes/General" data-tags=".NET2.0, C#2.0, .NET3.0, C#3.0, .NET3.5, C#, .NET, Dev, Intermediate, Advanced, C#4.0, .NET4,rating4.5">
                <noscript>
                 <a href="https://pubads.g.doubleclick.net/gampad/jump?iu=/6839/lqm.codeproject.site/General-Programming/Algorithms-Recipes/General&amp;sz=210x60&amp;c=838809"><img src="https://pubads.g.doubleclick.net/gampad/jump?iu=/6839/lqm.codeproject.site/General-Programming/Algorithms-Recipes/General&amp;sz=210x60&amp;c=838809" width="210px" height="60px" target="_blank"></a>

             <div id="ctl00_description" class="summary">
              An article on how to detect the language of a written text.
             </div>
             <span id="ctl00_thumbnailUrl" class="date" content="https://www.codeproject.com/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/Thumb-43198.gif"></span> 
            </div> 
            <div id="contentdiv" class="text"> 
             <ul class="download"> 
              <li><a href="/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/Babel.WinSample.zip">Download demo application - 516 KB</a></li> 
              <li><a href="/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/Babel.src.zip">Download source - 531 KB</a></li> 
             </ul> 
             <p><img height="405" src="/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/BabelSample.gif" width="600"></p> 
             <h2>Introduction</h2> 
             <p>Quite some time ago, I published an <a href="/KB/recipes/DetectEncoding.aspx">article</a> on how to detect the encoding of an given text. In this article, I describe the next step on the long way to text classification: the detection of language.</p> 
             <p>The given solution is based on n-gram and word occurrence comparison.</p> 
             <p>It is suitable for any language that uses words (this is actually not true for all languages).</p> 
             <p>Depending on the model and the length of the input text, the accuracy is between 70% (only short Norwegian, Swedisch and Danisch classified by the "all" model) and 99.8%, using the "default" model.</p> 
             <h2>Background</h2> 
             <p>The language detection of a written text is probably one of the most basic tasks in natural language processing (NLP). For any language depending processing of an unknown text, the first thing to know is which language the text is written in. Luckily, it is one of the easier challenges that NLP has to offer. The approach I have chosen to implement is widely known and pretty straightforward. The idea is that any language has a unique set of character (co-)occurrences.</p> 
             <p>The first step is to collect those statistics for all languages that should be detectable. This is not as easy as it may sound in the first place. The problem is to collect a large set of test data (plain text) that contains only one language and that is not domain specific. (Only newspaper articles may lack the use of the word “I” and direct speech. Using Shakespeare plays will not be the best approach to detect contemporary texts. Medical articles tend to contain too many domain specific terms which are not even language specific (major, minor, arteria etc…).) And if that would not be hard enough, the texts should not be copyrighted. (I am not sure if this is a true requirement. Are the results of statistical analytics of copyrighted texts also copyrighted?) I have chosen to use Wikipedia as my primary source. I had to do some filtering to "clean" the sources from the ever present English phrases that occur in almost any article – no matter what language they are written in (I actually used Babel itself to detect the English phrases). The clean up was in no way perfect. Wikipedia contains a lot of proper names (i.e., band names) that often contain a “the” or an “and”. This is why those words occur in many languages even if they are not part of the language. This must not necessarily be a disadvantage, because Anglicism is widely spread across many languages. I created three statistics for each language:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><strong>Character set</strong></li> 
              <p>Some languages have a very specific Character set (e.g., Chinese, Japanese, and Russian); for others, some characters give a good hint of what languages come in question (e.g., the German Umlauts).</p> 
              <li><strong>N-Grams</strong></li> 
              <p>After tokenizing the text into words (where applicable), the occurrences of each 1, 2, and 3-grams were counted. Some n-grams are very language specific (e.g., the "TH" in English).</p> 
              <li><strong>Word list</strong></li> 
              <p>The last source of disambiguation is the actually used words. Some languages (like Portuguese and Spanish) are almost identical in used characters and also the occurrences of the specific n-grams. Still, different words are used in different frequencies.</p> 
             </ul> 
             <p>A set of statistics is called a model. I have created some subsets of the "all" model that meet my needs the best (see table below). The "common" model contains the 10 most spoken languages in the world. The “small” and “default” are based on my usage scenarios. If you are from another part of the world, your preferences might be different. So please take no offence in my choice of what languages are contained in which model.</p> 
             <p>All statistics are ordered and ranked by their occurrences. Within the demo application, all models can be studied in detail. Classification of an unknown text is straightforward. The text is tokenized and the three tables for the statistics are generated. The result table is compared to all tables in the model, and a distance is calculated. The comparison table from the model that has the smallest distance to the unknown text is most likely the language of the text.</p> 
             <p><a title="Click to enlarge" href="/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/ModelSample.gif"><img height="256" src="/KB/recipes/DialogueMaster_Babel/ModelSample_small.gif" width="600" border="0"></a></p> 
             <div class="Caption">
              Sample model
             </div> 
             <h2>Using the code</h2> 
             <h3>Quick word about the code</h3> 
             <p>Babel is part of a larger project. I wanted the Babel assembly to work stand-alone. Since some of the used classes originally were scattered across many assemblies, I used the define "<code>_DIALOGUEMASTER</code>" to indicate whether to use the DialogueMaster™ assemblies or implement (a probably simpler) version in place.</p> 
             <p>Any impartand DialogueMaster™ class is remotable. The clients need only one assembly containing all the interface definitions. This is why Babel uses so many interfaces where they might seem to bloat the code in the first place. Additionally, DialogueMaster™ offers lots of PerformanceCounters. I chose to omit them for an easier usage of the assembly (no installation and no admin rights needed).</p> 
             <p>What I actually want to say is: the code is not as readable and clean as it could (and should) be.</p> 
             <h3>Classify text</h3> 
             <p>Usage of the code is straightforward. First, you must chose (or create your own) model. The <code>ClassifyText</code> method returns a <code>ICategoryList</code> which is a list of <code>ICateogry</code> (name-score pairs) items sorted descending by their score.</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> System;

<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"></span>
<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> Most simple samlple</span>
<span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"></span>

<span class="code-keyword">class</span> Program
{
    <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
    {
        DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel model = DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel._AllModel;
        <span class="code-sdkkeyword">String</span> s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        <span class="code-keyword">while</span> (s.Length <span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span> <span class="code-digit">0</span>)
        {
            DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategoryList result = model.ClassifyText(s, <span class="code-digit">10</span>);
            <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategory category <span class="code-keyword">in</span> result)
            {
                System.Console.Out.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string"> {0} : {1}"</span>, category.Name, category.Score);
            }

            s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        }
    }
}</pre> 
             <h2>Define your own model</h2> 
             <h3>From existing set</h3> 
             <p>To define your own model from the existing set of languages, simply create a new <code>BabelModel</code> and add the required languages from the <code>_AllModel</code>.</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">class</span> Program2
{
    <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
    {
        <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> Create a custom model </span>
        DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel model = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel();
        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">de"</span>, DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel._AllModel[<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">de"</span>]);
        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">en"</span>, DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel._AllModel[<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">en"</span>]);
        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">sv"</span>, DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel._AllModel[<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">sv"</span>]);

        <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ask the user for some input</span>
        <span class="code-sdkkeyword">String</span> s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        <span class="code-keyword">while</span> (s.Length <span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span> <span class="code-digit">0</span>)
        {
            <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> classify it </span>
            DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategoryList result = model.ClassifyText(s, <span class="code-digit">10</span>);
            <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> and dump the result</span>
            <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategory category <span class="code-keyword">in</span> result)
            {
                System.Console.Out.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string"> {0} : {1}"</span>, category.Name, category.Score);
            }

            s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        }
    }
}</pre> 
             <h3>Add new language</h3> 
             <p>To add a new language is pretty straightforward. All you need is some learn data text.</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">class</span> Program3
{
    <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
    {
        <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> Create a custom model </span>
        DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel model = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel();
        TokenTable klingonTable = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> TokenTable(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> FileInfo(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">LearnData\\Klingon.txt"</span>));
        TokenTable vulcanTable = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> TokenTable(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> FileInfo(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">LearnData\\Vulcan.txt"</span>));

        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">kling"</span>, klingonTable);
        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">vulcan"</span>, klingonTable);
        model.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">en"</span>, DialogueMaster.Babel.BabelModel._AllModel[<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">en"</span>]);


        <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> ask the user for some input</span>
        <span class="code-sdkkeyword">String</span> s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        <span class="code-keyword">while</span> (s.Length <span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span> <span class="code-digit">0</span>)
        {
            <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> classify it </span>
            DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategoryList result = model.ClassifyText(s, <span class="code-digit">10</span>);
            <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> and dump the result</span>
            <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (DialogueMaster.Classification.ICategory category <span class="code-keyword">in</span> result)
            {
                System.Console.Out.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string"> {0} : {1}"</span>, category.Name, category.Score);
            }

            s = System.Console.ReadLine();
        }
    }
}</pre>

            <h2 id="ctl00_AboutHeading">About the Author</h2> 
            <div class="author-wrapper"> 
             <div class="pic-wrapper"> 
              <img id="ctl00_AboutAuthorRptr_ctl00_AboutAuthor_memberPhoto" class="profile-pic" src="https://www.codeproject.com/script/Membership/ProfileImages/{51B3BF2A-CFDC-41CB-9E5C-95AE29819308}.jpg" style="border-width:0px;transform:rotate(-4deg);"> 
             </div> 
             <div class="container-member"> 
              <b><a id="ctl00_AboutAuthorRptr_ctl00_AboutAuthor_memberProfileLink" class="author" href="/Members/Carsten-Zeumer">Carsten Zeumer</a></b> 
              <table class="extended"> 
               <tbody>
                <tr> 
                 <td rowspan="2" nowrap valign="middle"> </td> 
                 <td width="100%"> 
                  <div class="company"> 
                   <span id="ctl00_AboutAuthorRptr_ctl00_AboutAuthor_memberJobTitle">Software Developer (Senior)</span> 
                   <span id="ctl00_AboutAuthorRptr_ctl00_AboutAuthor_memberCompany"></span> 
                  </div> </td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td> <span id="ctl00_AboutAuthorRptr_ctl00_AboutAuthor_memberLocation">Germany <img src="/script/Geo/Images/DE.gif" alt="Germany" width="16px" height="11px"></span> </td> 
                </tr>

             </div> 
             <div class="description">
               Carsten started programming Basic and Assembler back in the 80’s when he got his first C64. After switching to a x86 based system he started programming in Pascal and C. He started Windows programming with the arrival of Windows 3.0. After working for various internet companies developing a linguistic text analysis and classification software for 
              <a rel="nofollow" href="http://25h-communications.com/">25hours communications</a> he is now working as a contractor.
              <br> 
              <br> Carsten lives in Hamburg, Germany with his wife and five children. 
             </div>

                      <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="4491772" parent="4491753" thread="4491753" href="/Messages/4491772/Re-change-the-model.aspx">Re: change the model</a> <a onclick="return forumControl29908736.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>
                       <div class="mobile-only"> 
                        <span class="author">Carsten Zeumer</span>

                 <tr id="F4491772_h1" class="content selected" style="display:none;"> 
                  <td class="normal" width="100%">
                   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">

                     <tr valign="top"> 
                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:38px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="90293" msgid="4491772" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="38px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl29908736.SwitchMessage(null,4491753);" href="/Messages/4491753/change-the-model.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Hi Mamoooshi,<br> <br> the model is actually not ment to be altered manually. Even though you can simply load a model, Change, delete or add entries to the tables and store it back you will most probably not be able to figure resonable values for the relative number of occurences.<br> <br> Please be also aware, that the models do only contain the top n words of each language. So most probably the words you are missing are not among the top occurrences within my learn data (Wikipedia). Normally you should not need to add words to the corpus, since they are mostly used to disambiguate between very similar languages (swedisch, norge and danish).<br> <br> What you could do, would be to create your own language corpus, that is closer to the kind of texts you try to detect. Even though, the Wikipedia corpus is huge, it is the best for any use-case. I.E. if you detect mostly colloquial text you might get better results with you own model.<br> 
                               <div class="signature">
                                /cadi
                                <br> 
                                <br> 24 hours is not enough
                               </div><br></td>

For example, text of 30% English, 30% Russian and 30% Arabic recognized as [en:30.87][ru:28.23][nl:21.08][no:19.82] (Arabic is not in the results). <br> Is it possible to config this tool to work better with multi-languages texts? Or is this fixed in another version?<br> Thank you.<br></td>

                               </div>Hi yevgeniya30,<br> <br> I'd make to suggestions to improve detection rate for your scenario:<br> <br> - Split the text in pragraphs or sentences. Most likely the the different languages will align to them.<br> - reduce the detectable languages to a subset that ist most likely to occur in your text<br> <br> also keep in mind, that the default algorythm does not analyze the hole text but only the first n(dont remember the exact number) charactes. This might explain why arabic is not in your list.<br>

                                /cadi

                               </div>I've fixed this by calling BuildCharTable() for new added languages:<br> <br> TokenTable georgianTable = new TokenTable(new FileInfo("georgian.txt"));<br> georgianTable.BuildCharTable();<br> s_AllModel.Add("ka", georgianTable);<br></td>

                               </div>Hi Nash,<br> <br> since it is a task given by your lecturer I guess she wants you to learn something along the way to solve the problem <img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/smiley_wink.gif" align="top" alt="Wink | ;)"> <br> <br> I actually can't go more into depth than the article already does. You should try to read the article and the source once more. The idea is to find the one that matches (statistically) best one of the tables in the model. If you have only one language it will most probably hit very often.....<br>

                               </div>Hi Patrice,<br> <br> the source code is complete. The babel assembly and the sample compile without problems. <br> The missing projects can safely be ignored. This is because Babel is part of a bigger project.<br> <br> The wordlists are within the all.Model resource.<br> <br> You can extract the word list like this:<br> <br> <pre><span class="code-keyword">using</span> System;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> DialogueMaster.Babel;
&nbsp;
<span class="code-keyword">namespace</span> WinSample
{
    <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">class</span> Program
    {
        [STAThread]
        <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main()
        {
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (<span class="code-keyword">string</span> lang <span class="code-keyword">in</span> BabelModel._AllModel.Keys)
            {
                System.Console.Out.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Most common words for: "</span> + lang);
                ITokenTable wordTable = BabelModel._AllModel[lang].WordTable;
&nbsp;
                <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (ITokenStats wordStat <span class="code-keyword">in</span> wordTable.Values)
                {
                    System.Console.Out.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">{0}\t{1}\t{2}"</span>,
                        wordStat.Rank,  wordStat.Token, wordStat.Occurences);
                }
            }
&nbsp;
        }
    }
}</pre> <br> <br> 
                               <div class="ForumSig">
                                /cadi
                                <br> 
                                <br> 24 hours is not enough

                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl29908736.SwitchMessage(null,3256132);" href="/Messages/3256132/Re-Word-list.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Hi Patrice,<br> <br> I am not sure if you are realy looking for the most common words, you try to filter out the noise words (words, you don't want to index). Actually it is almost the same but you might be more lucky to search the internet for noisword lists.<br> <br> But actually I doubt, that simply removing the noise leaves you with a proper index. From your sample I guess (my french is very poor) you want to extract the nouns. A word list won't do this. You need a POS-Tagger for the language at hand. I have one for english (BROWN), german (STTS) and danish (DK2000). Lacking any (free) french learndata (and the ability to understand french) I have none for french... Probably one of my next articles will cover the POS-Tagger.<br> <br> For a good keyword index I would suggest to use a POS-Tagger and then a good Parser/Chunker. Then you try to expand all pronomina and use some kind of summarizer. From the now condensed text try to extract the most common phrases... <br> <br> If you only want to have a search index, I'd suggest to have a close look at lucene. <br> <br>

                        function getVotesHistogram(objectId, objectTypeId, containerId, loadingId) {
                            if (!$('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested')){
                                $.ajax({
                                    url: '/script/Ratings/Ajax/Histogram.aspx?obid=' + objectId + '&obtid='+objectTypeId,
                                    success: function (data) {
                                        $('#' + containerId).html(data);
                                        $('#' + loadingId).hide();
                                    }
                                });
                                $('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested', 'true');
                            }
                        }
